<text>I just moved from Brooklyn to Los Angeles. I was a bit concerned about using this company at first after seeing some of the bad reviews but I did some research and this company seemed to have a good standing with BBB and it fit my budget so I thought I'd take the plunge. Judging by the reviews their San Francisco office doesn't seem to fair as well as the others.

I asked the movers to show up on the early side because I lived on a busy street. They came when I asked them to, which made it possible for them to park right out front my building. I only had to pay $1.25 for parking because they moved an entire 1 Bedroom Apt in an hour. (Not too much furniture, the only big things were the mattress, a kitchen counter, a desk, and a bed frame) Overall they moved 54 pieces for me.

I received an email from them every weekday letting me know where my stuff was. That was very comforting. My things arrived much sooner then I expected, it shipped on a Friday (Same day it got picked up), arrived in LA Thursday, and was dropped off Monday. (10 days over all - they could have come Saturday but it was inconvenient for me so they agreed on monday.)

The movers themselves were very polite and very friendly. They explained what they would do before they moved my stuff into the truck and when they unloaded it. They gave me the inventory from the pick up and let me check off things as they came into the house. They also called out the numbers on the boxes for me to help me find them on the inventory list. This made it so that I knew all of my stuff was in the house and I wasn't scrambling around to make sure I had everything.

I will say that a few of my boxes were a bit banged up but I think that would be common of moving that much stuff across the country. If I had moved it myself the same would have probably happened. Thankfully I packed my very fragile things in small boxes that I then put into a large box. Nothing was broken.

Overall I highly recommend California New York Express. I had a great experience and it made my move a lot less stressful.<//text>< gmap_id>

< text>
I had planned a move out west for a long while but was very skeptical about which company to hire due to the many horror stories you hear and read about on the Internet.  Being that this was a long distance move from one of  the two furthest endpoints in the country to the other, you can imagine my trepidation of having my furniture held hostage, last minute jacked-up prices or worse--lost/missing irreplaceable items.  So, I had whittled down my choices to three companies who were either recommended by friends or via the Internet.  Some had a mix of great and awful reviews, so it was still hard to judge who would be the better company to go with.   In the end, I chose CANY for one of the best reasons offered by Noel who was a charming guy in the NY office who presented an argument I couldn't refute--they have a presence on both the east and west coast, so you can be assured that they have staff that are answerable to problems that come up even after the move, being that they are employees of the company and have a vested interest in doing the right thing.  Otherwise, you can have stellar service moving you and then gorillas rounded up at the other side of the move to unpack you.  My friend in Boston had that happen with another moving company.  Move went off seamlessly until they came to his house.  Since the company was a NY-based company, they had no workers in Boston and hired day laborers who didn't really care about anything other than being paid for the day and so his priceless items were juggled like in a circus act and many things were damaged on his move-in day.  Not a scenario I want to envision or have to encounter on my own.

The move itself--five full days to pack up 35 years of stuff was daunting, but Silas, the foreman was outstanding.  Most of the guys were great (shout out to Tony who killed many trees with tons of paper used to pack  my stuff that took eons to unwrap and more time to unload in Sanitation, but came out undamaged).  A few workers were eh-eh (don't know who in particular put a jar of fish with my books...The jar broke, of course and my books smell fishy!), but overall a nightmare process that I sweated on for months came to an end within a mere 4 days after our arrival.  There were some damages (broken items on the premises itself and others that came damaged) but nothing that couldn't be fixed or repaired.  I did have insurance but some of the items were not covered (for whatever reasons) and another shout out to Perry in the CA Claims dept--who went over and beyond reasonable charges and ensured that I was covered for those items insurance didn't pick up.  All in, nothing was missing out of 548 items which in itself is a miracle.  True, some of the items were misplaced (i.e. dining room tagged items were stuck behind a box in one of the bedrooms and not found till months later), but everything was accounted for at the end of the day.

Even though they were the costliest of the three estimates I had received (so no vacation for the next 5 years!!), I am glad I chose CANY. I plan to move again in the near future and hope that the experience will be as good the second time around with CANY.< /text>

These guys were great. I was in a bind three days out from move day. (I had issue with other company.) California New York Express came through last minute. Not only were they on time for pick up but delivered our stuff within 6 days. Not business days. They did it in six days...NY to LA. Crazy. My wife and I were kind of blown away by them.  And the price Josh quoted me on phone remained the same the entire way. Moving companies can hit you with charges on the day.They all do it.  We've moved a bunch in the last two years so we're a bit more experienced than most. Before we moved we pretty much knew exactly what stuff we had. (That always helps...everyone needs to be on the same page or else that price will change.) In our case, some of our inventory changed the day before the move, I called Josh and told him of inventory changes. He adjusted price to reflect and it was smooth sailing from there. Remember to ask when booking your move about what charges that could come up on the day. Like Long Carry...if the movers have to carry stuff for more than 100 yards (each company has different amount of yards for it to be considered long carry. And each company does it.) Some charge for stairs and depending on where you live they might have to get a smaller truck to deliver your stuff than a 16 wheeler. If they do need smaller truck you'll get hit with a charge for that too. Just do your research and ask, the all important question, "What kind of charges can I get hit with other than the move itself? Josh at California NY Express will be more than upfront. The delivery teams on both sides of the coast were great. Total pro's and just a bunch of good dudes. We lucked out with these guys and I couldn't recommend them more highly.< /Review>

< Text>
CA-NY Express Movers are excellent communicators. They make you feel comfortable in preparing for the move, communicate well during the move and are prompt with the delivery.

However, there are 3 things they are really bad at:
1. Packing your stuff
2. Moving your stuff
3. Resolving issues when they break your stuff

We moved from the Bay Area to NYC with CA-NY Express Movers. Having lived in temp accommodation for over a month, we were really looking forward to moving into our own apartment with our own stuff and get the feeling of being at home in a new city.

The delivery team arrived on time and started unloading, after accepting full payment, of course. As the first pieces of furniture starting coming in, my heart started sinking.

We immediately noticed broken furniture and damaged cartons. The delivery crew foreman himself told us that this was really bad packing and that they often see this with the California packing crew. So after paying to pack  and move the furniture, we had to buy the ENTIRE FURNITURE FOR TWO BEDROOMS. Yes, thatâ€™s right, two broken beds, two night stands broken, one chest of drawers broken and unstable. And that was all the bedroom furniture we moved an nothing survived the move â€“ so basically we shouldnâ€™t have bothered!!!

Then I start opening the torn/tattered cartons. My delicate show pieces â€“ Crystal, Porcelain, Stained Glass, were literally DUMPED in cartons (And I specifically showed the pieces that required extra care to your moving staff who came to pack). How they survived without breaking is surprising. Horrible packing, no fragile tag.

Next, moving on to the Wardrobe boxes â€“ loose shoes just tossed at the bottom of the carton with my coats on top. To add to that, my umbrellas and other products were thrown in between shoes. I'm just going to guess  these guys who packed my stuff travel with their dirty used shoes just packed in between their clean clothes. To me that is disgusting. Shoes should have been packed separately.

I explicitly mention that my Heeled shoes need care â€“ but it didnâ€™t matter, things were tossed in and my expensive shoes are now damaged.

Multiple items were packed around my TV in the TV box so now the back has a huge dent.

And through all this, I swear I kept my cool. What made me lose it is that toilet waste bins and the bathroom and toilet rugs were packed with my kitchen items. And just in case that was not enough - They packed the 2nd bathroom stuff including a waste bin and shower curtain with my babyâ€™s clothes, toys, sippy cup!

< Review>
Moving an apartment of furniture cross-country by myself from New York to California was a daunting process. I compared prices between a number of moving companies and was impressed by the affordable rates provided by CANYX. Once I requested a quote, I began a line of communication with a very helpful customer service representative at the company, who promptly answered all and any questions I had via email and phone. After deciding to use CANYX, the process to organize my move went smoothly, with an easily accessible online inventory that I could update up to 72 hours before the move. I was also able to schedule the pickup and delivery dates with no problem, and I booked about a month in advance to my move.

On the day of the move, the movers arrived in the provided time frame and Ivan (I think!), the man I assumed to be in charge, went through everything with me beforehand and afterwards. He and his two other movers were all extremely polite and incredibly efficient, packing and wrapping everything carefully, and even dissembling a patio table.

After they left, I received frequent email updates informing me of the progression of the shipment, and in about week, my belongings were in California ready to be delivered. Because I hadn't moved yet, I authorized my roommate in Los Angeles to oversee the delivery, and she also reported to me that the movers were very friendly, quick, and efficient, and arrived during the designated window.

A cross-country move is incredibly stressful, and I am so grateful to CANYX for making it as painless and easy as possible!</Review>

<date>1558125145083</date><Rating>5</Rating><Review>Read a lot of negative reviews and was skeptical. Since I live near by, I drove to his shop to visit. First impression, Tony runs a very busy and lean organization, I can understand why some people may have had trouble getting through on the phone. I found Tony to by extremely knowledgeable, courteous, and non-stop-hard-working. We talked about what parts I needed, he checked warehouse availability and said he would be placing an order in about a week or so. I was in no hurry for the parts and in about a week or so, the parts were in and I picked them up. He does stock some parts but is not a warehouse of every part in the catalog, just to be clear. He seems to order parts for his customers when he has enough to minimize the shipping cost to his shop. That means cost savings to his customers. If you don't need your parts over-night and would like to save money on your project, RPS is the right place to get your parts. I would suggest to ask about availability before you order to avoid back order issues. If you need your parts in a hurry, ask before you place your order. I will be a return customer.</Review>< Pictures>

<text>I am in  CO restoring a '63 Ranchero, and needed a gas tank and sending unit. RPS was one of the only places I found selling a complete kit (tank, filler neck and gaskets, sending unit, lock ring) and for a better price than anywhere else I found. I had some concerns based on all the negative reviews, which mostly seem related to the time to fulfill orders. I called first, not expecting an answer based on the reviews, but Tony (I assume it was Tony) answered the first call, and explained the part ships direct from the manufacturer and would ship the next business day.  I ordered it that day on the RPS website, and sure enough Monday I got a notice it had shipped. It arrived shortly after, and was the exact part I needed and expected, but the lock ring for the tank seemed to be missing. Again I called RPS (on a Saturday) and my call was answered on the first try. Tony explained that this manufacturer often tapes rings and gaskets inside boxes. Sure enough the lock ring and an extra gasket were taped on the underside of the bottom inside flap of the box, making it very hard to find unless you disassemble the box; probably would have never found it and thrown the box out with the ring if Tony didnt know that this particular manufacturer did that. I really am surprised by the negative comments as my experience was great, and I'll use RPS again for other hard to find parts.  It seems as one other commenter said this is a specialty operation and can take longer at times, but if you are not expecting Amazon-like fulfillment times I'd recommend RPS to anyone based on my experience< /text><Pics>None< /Pics><Response>None</Response><gmapID>0x808f91250df604f5:0xef1ef4eb67a9ba4a</gmapID></record></dataset><record>

< text>
WOW..... So this just hapened. This has to be the WORST dining experience I have ever had. Normally when we eat here we see Lenny walking around or hanging out. He has never just randomly come over to his tables and introduced himself or asked how we are. Tonight was different. We ordered a full rack of ribs (to share). We split 1/2 smoked whiskey and half smoked raspberry and ordered an extra mashed potatoes. Our food comes and I was not impressed. I ask my mom how her ribs are.. She told me that she thought that they were "stringy and a bit tough". I then said to her. "I don't like mine either". The ribs are not easy to bite and I felt they were tough and stringy as well. We both agreed that the mashed potatoes were good. We called over our server and let him know that we were not happy with the food and could we please get something else. I sat and watched as he let Lenny know. Lenny shook his head no and then waived the young kid off. A few minutes later Lenny comes out of the kitchen holding our plates. He sets one in front of me and one in front of my mom. He very nicely let us know that he personally tried the ribs and that "there is nothing wrong with them." He let us know that they actually were "more tender than usual." He explained his smoking process (I, as a chef am well aware but was polite and let him continue). So my mother said... "So you are trying to tell us that you aren't going to let us get something else?" I knew that the minute he put our food back on the table in front of us.  Lenny told us that "if there was something wrong with the food" he would be "happy to replace" it. However the ribs are just the way they always are served. He said to us "I can take 20% off your bill if that helps". WOW... "helps what" is what I wanted to say. I told him "it's not a financial issue it's an issue that we don't like the ribs and neither of us are happy." Lenny just reiterated that the ribs are the way they should be. I told him that I respect his decision but disagree with how he is handling the situation. I told him I understand as a chef and business owner but sometimes you need to take one for the team to make the customer happy as opposed to losing business. He just looked at me. I said, "well I won't be eating this can I have our check" my mother asked for the food to be boxed up since she was paying for it anyway. Me personally.. I was fine to leave it on the table. Now mind you... The restaurant is completely empty except for a man who had just walked in before Lenny came to our table to give us back our food. As Lenny walked away I looked at the man who had watched and listened to the entire exchange. He has his mouth gaping and shook his head. Got up from his table and walked out. YES HE LEFT. So.... We paid for this awful food and gave the server a $10 tip. He was as nice as can be. He told me several things but for fear that he may lose his job I won't put it on blast. I came home and made some eggs for dinner. I let Lenny know that we drove across the valley and would never be coming back. He had no reaction.  SHAME ON YOU LENNY... this is what happens when your EGO is more important than your guest's. Lenny should hang a sign on the door.. "If you don't like my food... LEAVE"<//text>

< text>
My wife and I went to Lenny's to celebrate our 24th anniversary.  Outstanding food, great decor, and friendly servers and employees.

The food is borderline upscale gourmet and the presentation is outstanding.  We got the Tres Quesadillas and they were presented with vibrant colored tortillas with sauces accenting the color for a feast of the eyes as well as mouth.

The house mop sauce is a tangy mustard based sauce that would be at home in Kansas City.  Think Gates.  But better.

All in all, a fantastic meal and a great night.  Thank you Lenny.<//text>

< userid>
108108786518294143367<//userid>
< name>
Quincy Freeman</name>
< Date>
1425788452220< /Date>
< rate>
2< /rate>
< review>
Sometimes you walk into a business, and you expect everything to go well. Nothing could not be truer about Lenny's Smokehouse BBQ in Chatsworth.  As I pull into the parking lot and I am greeted by the pit-master, I just knew everything would be alright.

I walk in without a reservation, and Grace immediately greeted me.  I should have had a reservation and felt wrong as she drilled that point home.  "Table for 2," I say calmly, amid the stern reprimand.  "There is about a 20 minute wait, sir" she stated.  My friend and I take a seat. In about 20 minutes or so, when Grace came to seat us, she informed me that the only seating available was outside.  I was against sitting outside because it was chilly, and I was coming down with what later become a cold.  Note to self: do not drive from Los Angeles to Phoenix, then back to Chatsworth for dinner with the air conditioner blowing in your face.  I eventually relented and sat outside. To her credit, once an inside table was available, she moved us.

My waitress' name was Brandy. She started off attentive and friendly. The hiccup came when she informed me that Lenny's does not have cornbread. I am not sure I have ever had that happen, no cornbread at a BBQ joint? I ordered a mixed full rack of the Raspberry Ribs and the Whiskey glazed ribs, with a side of Smoked Red Beans.  The fruit reduction sauce let me know immediately that this would not be a traditional BBQ dinner, but did not lead on the the surprise that would come later.  Furthermore not having cornbread saddened me, but Brandy offered to bring dinner rolls in their stead; unfortunately she may have forgotten to bring them.

I am no BBQ rib expert or pit master, but I do know overcooked and under-cooked meat. The rack of ribs I received from Lenny were both.  No smoke ring, hard pull on the under-cooked ribs, easy pull and even bone-cracking on the overcooked ones.  I will not bother asking where the dry rub was because it certainly was not on the ribs; perhaps the words [cajun rub, and special rub] were just used as a colorful description to distract you from the hoity-toity raspberry reduction sauce.  Or maybe the they were Kansas City ribs?  You know drenched in sauce with little meat or rub flavor profile.  The ambiance, live music, and overall feel of the restaurant is Southern, more specifically Nashville or Memphis.  So it seems we have a Tennessee restaurant in Southern California serving Kansas City-style BBQ ribs, I suppose I can get with that. We all go through an identity crisis at one time or another, right?

Lenny's Smokehouse BBQ looks great, and feels even better.  The setting makes you feel right at home, a Tennessee home; unfortunately the ribs are Kansas City not Tennessee.< /review>
